# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Leader Election Patterns Across K8s Ecosystem

## Your Task

Compare leader election implementations across kubernetes/kubernetes and etcd-io/etcd. Find Go source files in each repo that implement leader election: the lease-based election in k8s, the Raft-based leader in etcd, and how each handles leader failover and re-election.

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

56-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the comprehensive analysis of leader election implementations across both repositories and created the `answer.json` file at `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary of Findings

I've identified and documented **two fundamentally different approaches** to leader election:

### **Kubernetes: Lease-Based Model**
- Uses Kubernetes Lease API objects for coordination
- Time-based expiration mechanism (15s lease duration, 10s renewal deadline)
- Client-side polling and clock-based validation
- Simpler implementation suitable for application-level use
- Found in: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/`

### **etcd: Raft Consensus Model**
- Uses Raft consensus algorithm for cluster-wide agreement
- Millisecond-scale heartbeat-based detection (100ms typical)
- Quorum-based voting and strong consistency guarantees
- PreVote optimization to reduce disruptions from flaky nodes
- Graceful leadership transfer mechanism
- Found in: `server/etcdserver/raft.go` and `server/etcdserver/server.go`

### **Key Deliverables**
The answer file includes:
- **9 critical files** from both repositories
- **23 key symbols** (interfaces, structs, functions)
- **11-step call chains** showing execution flow for both implementations
- **Detailed narrative** explaining failover mechanisms and re-election handling
- **Comparison table** highlighting architectural differences

The analysis reveals that Kubernetes delegates leader election to its underlying etcd cluster (which itself uses Raft), while etcd implements direct Raft-based consensus for cluster leadership, providing faster failover detection and automatic quorum-based re-election.

Election\\n\\nKubernetes implements leader election using a **lease resource mechanism** in the coordination.v1 API. The implementation is found across multiple files:\\n\\n**Core Components:**\\n\\n1. **ResourceLock Interface** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/interface.go:81-100): Defines the abstract interface for locking mechanisms with four key operations:\\n   - `Get(ctx)`: Retrieve the current LeaderElectionRecord from the lease\\n   - `Create(ctx, ler)`: Create a new lease with election record\\n   - `Update(ctx, ler)`: Update the existing lease\\n   - `RecordEvent(s)`: Record events for auditing\\n\\n2. **LeaseLock Implementation** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/leaselock.go): The concrete implementation stores leader information in Kubernetes Lease objects:\\n   - LeaderElectionRecord contains: HolderIdentity, LeaseDurationSeconds, AcquireTime, RenewTime, LeaderTransitions\\n   - Conversion functions (LeaseSpecToLeaderElectionRecord, LeaderElectionRecordToLeaseSpec) bridge Kubernetes API objects and election records\\n\\n3. **LeaderElector Main Loop** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go:211-312):\\n   - `Run()`: Entry point that calls acquire(), then renew() loop\\n   - `acquire()`: Attempts to acquire leadership by polling tryAcquireOrRenew() with RetryPeriod jitter\\n   - `renew()`: Maintains leadership by renewing the lease within RenewDeadline, loses leadership if renewal fails\\n   - Election timers: LeaseDuration (15s), RenewDeadline (10s), RetryPeriod (2s)\\n\\n4. **Coordinated Leader Election** (pkg/controlplane/controller/leaderelection/election.go): Extends basic election with:\\n   - Multiple candidates (LeaseCandidate objects) compete for a single Lease\\n   - Strategy selection: OldestEmulationVersion or other strategies\\n   - Lease expiration check (isLeaseExpired): Compares RenewTime + LeaseDurationSeconds against current time\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism:**\\n- Failover is time-based: When the current leader fails to renew the lease within RenewDeadline, the lease is considered expired\\n- Other candidates detect expiration after LeaseDuration passes\\n- Re-election happens automatically when tryAcquireOrRenew() succeeds for a non-leader\\n- No explicit quorum requirement; client-side clock-based checking\\n\\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd uses **Raft consensus algorithm** for leader election, integrated directly into the core cluster management. The implementation spans:\\n\\n1. **Raft Node Wrapper** (server/etcdserver/raft.go:80-155):\\n   - `raftNode struct`: Wraps the Raft library's consensus implementation\\n   - `newRaftNode()`: Initializes Raft node with configuration\\n   - Manages ticker, apply channels, read states, and snapshot channels\\n   - Contains `raft.Node` interface for stepping through Raft state machine\\n\\n2. **Raft Ready Handler** (server/etcdserver/raft.go:173-339): The main event loop:\\n   - Processes `raft.Ready()` events containing committed entries and state changes\\n   - Detects leader changes via `SoftState.Lead` field\\n   - Updates leadership state and metrics (isLeader, hasLeader, leaderChanges)\\n   - Handles leader failover: When SoftState.Lead changes, calls `updateLeadership(newLeader)`\\n   - Leader sends messages to followers; followers process append entries and respond\\n\\n3. **Election Configuration** (server/config/config.go:86-117, server/embed/config.go:186-307):\\n   - `ElectionTicks`: Number of ticks for election timeout (default 10)\\n   - `TickMs`: Heartbeat interval (milliseconds)\\n   - `InitialElectionTickAdvance`: Fast-forwards election ticks on startup to speed up initial leader election\\n   - `PreVote`: Optional pre-vote phase to reduce disruptions from flaky nodes\\n   - Election timeout calculated as: ElectionTicks * TickMs\\n\\n4. **Leadership Detection** (server/etcdserver/server.go:925-942):\\n   - `Lead()` method returns the current leader ID from Raft status\\n   - Leadership verified through linearizable read (consensus-based confirmation)\\n   - `TryTransferLeadershipOnShutdown()`: Graceful leadership transfer during shutdown\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism:**\\n- **Automatic Election**: When a leader fails:\\n  1. Followers stop receiving heartbeats within ElectionTicks\\n  2. A follower becomes a candidate and requests votes\\n  3. Quorum of nodes votes for candidate, who becomes new leader\\n  4. New leader sends heartbeats to establish authority\\n  5. Election timeout is reset\\n\\n- **PreVote Optimization** (CHANGELOG-3.4.md): Introduced to handle disruptive nodes\\n  - Candidate first runs pre-vote phase to check vote feasibility\\n  - Reduces unnecessary term increments from flaky rejoining nodes\\n  - Prevents cascading re-elections\\n\\n- **Election Tick Adjustment** (CHANGELOG-3.1.md, server/config/config.go): Handles restart scenarios\\n  - InitialElectionTickAdvance=true: Fast-forwards election ticks on startup\\n  - On restart: Adjusts ticks with multiple ticks remaining (not just 1)\\n  - Gives leader more time to establish authority before disruptive followers trigger new elections\\n\\n- **Leadership Transfer** (server/etcdserver/server.go:1280-1273): Graceful transfer\\n  - `TransferLeadership()`: Current leader explicitly transfers to chosen transferee\\n  - Used during rolling upgrades and graceful shutdown\\n  - Ensures continuity without election disruption\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |\\n|--------|-----------|------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Time-based lease expiration | Raft consensus voting |\\n| **Consensus** | Client-side observation, no quorum | Quorum-based (Raft majority) |\\n| **Failover** | Passive: lease expires, others detect | Active: election votes replace leader |\\n| **Detection Time** | LeaseDuration (15s typical) | ElectionTicks * TickMs (100ms typical) |\\n| **State Storage** | Kubernetes API (etcd-backed) | Internal Raft log |\\n| **Re-election** | Any candidate can acquire after expiry | Quorum votes on new leader |\\n| **Graceful Shutdown** | Release lease (1s duration) | TransferLeadership to successor |\\n| **Disruption Handling** | Clock skew tolerance via JitterFactor | PreVote mechanism |\\n\\nBoth implementations ensure exactly-one leader is actively managing critical state, but Kubernetes relies on the underlying Kubernetes API server's etcd cluster (which uses Raft!) for coordination, while etcd itself uses direct Raft consensus for cluster-wide agreement.\"\n}\n",

\"TryTransferLeadershipOnShutdown\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"## Leader Election Comparison: Kubernetes (Lease-based) vs etcd (Raft-based)\\n\\n### Kubernetes: Lease-Based Leader Election\\n\\nKubernetes implements leader election using a **lease resource mechanism** in the coordination.v1 API. The implementation is found across multiple files:\\n\\n**Core Components:**\\n\\n1. **ResourceLock Interface** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/interface.go:81-100): Defines the abstract interface for locking mechanisms with four key operations:\\n   - `Get(ctx)`: Retrieve the current LeaderElectionRecord from the lease\\n   - `Create(ctx, ler)`: Create a new lease with election record\\n   - `Update(ctx, ler)`: Update the existing lease\\n   - `RecordEvent(s)`: Record events for auditing\\n\\n2. **LeaseLock Implementation** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/leaselock.go): The concrete implementation stores leader information in Kubernetes Lease objects:\\n   - LeaderElectionRecord contains: HolderIdentity, LeaseDurationSeconds, AcquireTime, RenewTime, LeaderTransitions\\n   - Conversion functions (LeaseSpecToLeaderElectionRecord, LeaderElectionRecordToLeaseSpec) bridge Kubernetes API objects and election records\\n\\n3. **LeaderElector Main Loop** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go:211-312):\\n   - `Run()`: Entry point that calls acquire(), then renew() loop\\n   - `acquire()`: Attempts to acquire leadership by polling tryAcquireOrRenew() with RetryPeriod jitter\\n   - `renew()`: Maintains leadership by renewing the lease within RenewDeadline, loses leadership if renewal fails\\n   - Election timers: LeaseDuration (15s), RenewDeadline (10s), RetryPeriod (2s)\\n\\n4. **Coordinated Leader Election** (pkg/controlplane/controller/leaderelection/election.go): Extends basic election with:\\n   - Multiple candidates (LeaseCandidate objects) compete for a single Lease\\n   - Strategy selection: OldestEmulationVersion or other strategies\\n   - Lease expiration check (isLeaseExpired): Compares RenewTime + LeaseDurationSeconds against current time\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism:**\\n- Failover is time-based: When the current leader fails to renew the lease within RenewDeadline, the lease is considered expired\\n- Other candidates detect expiration after LeaseDuration passes\\n- Re-election happens automatically when tryAcquireOrRenew() succeeds for a non-leader\\n- No explicit quorum requirement; client-side clock-based checking\\n\\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd uses **Raft consensus algorithm** for leader election, integrated directly into the core cluster management. The implementation spans:\\n\\n1. **Raft Node Wrapper** (server/etcdserver/raft.go:80-155):\\n   - `raftNode struct`: Wraps the Raft library's consensus implementation\\n   - `newRaftNode()`: Initializes Raft node with configuration\\n   - Manages ticker, apply channels, read states, and snapshot channels\\n   - Contains `raft.Node` interface for stepping through Raft state machine\\n\\n2. **Raft Ready Handler** (server/etcdserver/raft.go:173-339): The main event loop:\\n   - Processes `raft.Ready()` events containing committed entries and state changes\\n   - Detects leader changes via `SoftState.Lead` field\\n   - Updates leadership state and metrics (isLeader, hasLeader, leaderChanges)\\n   - Handles leader failover: When SoftState.Lead changes, calls `updateLeadership(newLeader)`\\n   - Leader sends messages to followers; followers process append entries and respond\\n\\n3. **Election Configuration** (server/config/config.go:86-117, server/embed/config.go:186-307):\\n   - `ElectionTicks`: Number of ticks for election timeout (default 10)\\n   - `TickMs`: Heartbeat interval (milliseconds)\\n   - `InitialElectionTickAdvance`: Fast-forwards election ticks on startup to speed up initial leader election\\n   - `PreVote`: Optional pre-vote phase to reduce disruptions from flaky nodes\\n   - Election timeout calculated as: ElectionTicks * TickMs\\n\\n4. **Leadership Detection** (server/etcdserver/server.go:925-942):\\n   - `Lead()` method returns the current leader ID from Raft status\\n   - Leadership verified through linearizable read (consensus-based confirmation)\\n   - `TryTransferLeadershipOnShutdown()`: Graceful leadership transfer during shutdown\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism:**\\n- **Automatic Election**: When a leader fails:\\n  1. Followers stop receiving heartbeats within ElectionTicks\\n  2. A follower becomes a candidate and requests votes\\n  3. Quorum of nodes votes for candidate, who becomes new leader\\n  4. New leader sends heartbeats to establish authority\\n  5. Election timeout is reset\\n\\n- **PreVote Optimization** (CHANGELOG-3.4.md): Introduced to handle disruptive nodes\\n  - Candidate first runs pre-vote phase to check vote feasibility\\n  - Reduces unnecessary term increments from flaky rejoining nodes\\n  - Prevents cascading re-elections\\n\\n- **Election Tick Adjustment** (CHANGELOG-3.1.md, server/config/config.go): Handles restart scenarios\\n  - InitialElectionTickAdvance=true: Fast-forwards election ticks on startup\\n  - On restart: Adjusts ticks with multiple ticks remaining (not just 1)\\n  - Gives leader more time to establish authority before disruptive followers trigger new elections\\n\\n- **Leadership Transfer** (server/etcdserver/server.go:1280-1273): Graceful transfer\\n  - `TransferLeadership()`: Current leader explicitly transfers to chosen transferee\\n  - Used during rolling upgrades and graceful shutdown\\n  - Ensures continuity without election disruption\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |\\n|--------|-----------|------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Time-based lease expiration | Raft consensus voting |\\n| **Consensus** | Client-side observation, no quorum | Quorum-based (Raft majority) |\\n| **Failover** | Passive: lease expires, others detect | Active: election votes replace leader |\\n| **Detection Time** | LeaseDuration (15s typical) | ElectionTicks * TickMs (100ms typical) |\\n| **State Storage** | Kubernetes API (etcd-backed) | Internal Raft log |\\n| **Re-election** | Any candidate can acquire after expiry | Quorum votes on new leader |\\n| **Graceful Shutdown** | Release lease (1s duration) | TransferLeadership to successor |\\n| **Disruption Handling** | Clock skew tolerance via JitterFactor | PreVote mechanism |\\n\\nBoth implementations ensure exactly-one leader is actively managing critical state, but Kubernetes relies on the underlying Kubernetes API server's etcd cluster (which uses Raft!) for coordination, while etcd itself uses direct Raft consensus for cluster-wide agreement.\"\n}\n",
